Friday, November 17, 2017 at 12:58pm EST
Apologies to my Denison brothers and sisters who already know this. My frat (Kappa Sigma) had "help" week, instead of "hell" week, for the pledges, where we cleaned and fixed-up our future living quarters. No abuse involved. We styled ourselves in opposition to the boorish macho posturing of some of the other houses but we paid a social cost for that. The majority of girls wanted to hang out with the "bad boys." We had a saying at the house: "Get drunk, abuse women, get laid." It wasn't an injunction. It was a lament about our frustration that bad behavior seemed to be rewarded elsewhere. I don't want to sound like I'm victim-blaming (or like a frustrated nerd. Well, I am a nerd), but women have a lot of power and should wield it. The culture will change when college women signal they won't put up with bad behavior. The Zeitgeist is shifting, allowing women to go public to shame predators. It's about time, bro. I'll reserve comment about the Times' inability to transliterate Greek letters. "NF MTGS?"

Thursday, November 16, 2017 at 8:48am EST
Some perspective on the new blood pressure guidelines. They’re based on a big “quality” study but the sample included only people already with “higher-than-average risk for cardiovascular events.” 92% of group that adhered to the old guidelines (less than 140 systolic) did NOT have an “event” and 94% of the group that adhered to the less-than-120 standard did not. Less alarming when you look at it that way.

Wednesday, November 15, 2017 at 9:54pm EST
So last night Pence says “let me share one anecdote that shows what a warm wonderful man the President is.” I’ll paraphrase for brevity but I think I’m being fair to the VP. “When the President was considering me for the running mate job, I felt it important that our families meet. He invited me to his club. We arrived Friday night but were not scheduled to meet until Saturday morning. We are in the dining room and the manager, Dave, comes up and says ‘how are you doing? Do you need anything? Mr. Trump called twice from his car to make sure you are settling in OK.’ I said, ‘that’s nice’ and Dave said, ‘Well, you know Mr. Trump.’ I said ‘I don’t.” The End.

Excuse me while I plug my Tesla into my solar roof. Zero emissions, Baby!

Dad is STILL around to tell the tale.

Sunday, March 5, 2017 at 10:45am EST
I'm reading a book liberated from my Dad's library, "Up Front" by Bill Maudlin. Maudlin was a celebrated army cartoonist of WWII. He depicted the life of the infantry "dogfaces," like my Dad, immortalized in the duo, Willie and Joe. His audience was the soldiers. When you're in combat you learn things nobody should have to learn, like how to identify artillery shells by the different sounds. Click on the photo if you can't see the text.

Monday, February 6, 2017 at 10:06am EST
From Wikipedia's Teddy Roosevelt entry: Roosevelt normally enjoyed very close relationships with the press...He drew the line, however, at expose-oriented scandal-mongering journalists...Roosevelt himself was not usually a target, but his speech in 1906 coined the term "muckraker" for unscrupulous journalists making wild charges. "The liar," he said, "is no whit better than the thief, and if his mendacity takes the form of slander he may be worse than most thieves." The press did briefly target Roosevelt in one instance. Ever since 1904, he had been periodically criticized for the manner in which he facilitated the Panama Canal. In the least judicious use of executive power, according to biographer Brands, Roosevelt, near the end of his term, demanded that the Justice Department bring charges of criminal libel against Joseph Pulitzer's New York World. The publication had accused him of "deliberate misstatements of fact" in defense of family members who were criticized as a result of the Panama affair. Though indictment was obtained, the case was ultimately dismissed in federal court—it was not a federal offense, but one enforceable at the state court level. The Justice Department had predicted that result, and had also advised Roosevelt accordingly.[189]

Dickens' "A Christmas Carol" makes a wry observation on the creditworthiness of the US in 1843. As Scrooge begins to doubt how much time is passing, he wonders what that means to due dates on his loan portfolio. A promise to pay "would have become a mere United States’ security if there were no days to count by."

Monday, December 5, 2016 at 9:41pm EST
Reading Dickens' "A Christmas Carol" at bedtime to the kids. The prose is great: "I don’t mean to say that I know, of my own knowledge, what there is particularly dead about a door-nail. I might have been inclined, myself, to regard a coffin-nail as the deadest piece of ironmongery in the trade. But the wisdom of our ancestors is in the simile; and my unhallowed hands shall not disturb it, or the Country’s done for. You will therefore permit me to repeat, emphatically, that Marley was as dead as a door-nail."

Saturday, December 3, 2016 at 12:29pm EST
I'm obsessed with this clock, recently acquired by The Met. It looks Art Deco modern but was made circa 1790! Like in 1920s America, Europe was overcome with a mania for ancient Egypt in the late 1700s, hence the motif. Made in Germany but the movement is a "Franklin." Ben invented this wacky 4-hours/1 full rotation movement as way to make cheaper clocks for the masses - it took fewer parts to build. It never caught on but it seems the Germans, like the French, were in love with all things Franklin. Ben was a European hero for inventing the lightning rod, which spared countless church spires.

In 1962 John F. Kennedy, whose campaign pledge was “get America moving again,” called for “an across-the-board, top-to-bottom cut in personal and corporate income taxes” to reform a system that “reduces the financial incentives for personal effort, investment, and risk-taking.” The economy grew strongly for years.

A friend I respect (all my facebook "friends" are actual friends) pointed out I am a privileged white man so it's easy for me to say "let's hope for the best." True. I have not walked a mile in non-privileged moccasins (though I was the nerd who was terrified of gym class). But perhaps some perspective from someone less close to it is still helpful. So I'll venture only this: The hearts of Americans, including most Trump (and Hillary) supporters, are kind and generous. The nut cases always shriek the loudest. America is not, and won't become, a dictatorship. "Checks and balances" are real. Inclusion and diversity are American values that have ebbed and flowed over the centuries. The river keeps rolling in the right direction though. No, it doesn't just happen. We have to keep pushing for it. I am with you.

Friday, November 11, 2016 at 9:29am EST
There's a picture somewhere of my dad in basic training, 1945, Fort Benning, GA. He's posing all cocky, action shot, with his M1 rifle. Two months later he's pinned down in a Bavarian potato field and gets shot. He was lucky. Spent six weeks in the hospital and by the time he rejoined his unit the war in Europe was over. Spent the rest of his tour flirting with the Frauleins, including my future mom! Thanks Dad!

Wonk time. I think the corporate tax rate should be cut. Okay, okay. Consider the source. Of course a privileged one-percenter would say that, but President Obama agrees with me! Why? Because lower corporate taxes lead to MORE jobs at HIGHER PAY for American workers. The empirical evidence is pretty solid, which is why both sides of the aisle support it. Simple, effective, market-based. Now consider the commercials Hillary is running about her economic plan. To achieve ostensibly the same result she wants to levy an exit tax on companies moving overseas and "use the money" for "job training." Friends, Hillary's plan is harmful and cynical. First, jobs are better than job training. Duh. This doesn't create ANY jobs. Second, it does create yet another government middle man with incentives to throw sand in the gears and slow growth. Third, this deliberately bad policy is out there because noises about punishment get more votes talking than about good policy. I prefer lighting candles than cursing the darkness. Vote Gary Johnson. #JohnsonWeld

Wednesday, May 4, 2016 at 9:19am EDT
Interesting dream last night. I was urban exploring an old railroad bridge (think Cleveland Flats) and, in a rush, a Carlos Castaneda moment, I had total consciousness of the entire rail *network*. The enormity of it. The juxtaposition of the rectilinearity of the trusses, bridges and tunnels against the swooping curves of the rails.It was beautiful and magnificent. I realized it was one of the wonders of the world. I was overcome with emotion. .... Then the dream morphed and I was standing in the same place but I was a character in a reality TV show and my explorations were fodder for internet mockery.

The Google doodle today commemorates Claude Shannon, who "founded" digital circuit design and information theory. He wrote "the most important masters thesis of the century." It's worth reading the Wikipedia entry because so much of the world we know is based on the principles this guy invented. He also invented the "useless machine." When you turn it on the only thing it does is turn itself off.

That bastard, Roland, who sat next to me in school, had the lunchbox. STINGRAY My kids today love it. Check the Barry Gray love theme https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8jrSupvayPU UFO Live action! I had forgotten that one. Thanks ,Wikipedia! SPACE 1999 Live action with Martin Landau! The special effects were Supermarionation all the way. TERRAHAWKS: My favorite from 80s (yes, I was a grown up then) My kids are scared of the Martian witch. They won't watch it with me. In glorious "HudsonColour." If you like "The Final Countdown" you'll love the theme music https://youtu.be/vZC9B0YJ8W8 Wikipedia says the Andersons produced 20 TV shows! The late Sylvia deserves extra credit for being a force in British TV production in her own right, long after divorcing Gerry.

For Downton Abbey fans, here the stakes are much higher. The tempests are not just in teapots.

Tuesday, April 28, 2015 at 5:55pm EDT
Went to the inaugural exhibition at the new Whitney museum, "America is Hard to See." Quite a good survey of many decades. I was struck by two phases of American turmoil, the depression of the 1930's and the Vietnam era. Artists in both era's were enraged by what they saw around them. I have to say though, the art of the 60s/70s was "pop art" as opposed to the "serious painting" of the 30's. The art of the 30's moved me more because it felt like the artists put more effort into their work and therefore had higher conviction in their message. A retrograde view, perhaps.

150 Years ago. Lee’s troops were paroled, mean­ing they could re­turn home, and were given ra­tions from Union wag­ons. Last fall I posted a pic of my garden cayenne peppers into a bottle of vodka and tequila. I can now post the results of the experiment. COLOR: vodka has a reddish tinge. Pepper still red. Tequila has barely any color but pepper is completely bleached! FLAVOR: vodka has modest heat. Tequila has almost no pepper flavor. EFFECT: vodka, gets you wasted. Tequila, gets you wasted.

We ask for low taxes but ex­pect more gov­ern­ment services. We de­mand pro­tec­tion while in­sist­ing on pri­vacy. Tuesday, August 26, 2014 at 8:20pm EDT
Too geek cool. Image stabilized iPhone video. Video stabilizing is usually with steadicams or in post processing using image processing to infer how the camera is moving. The iPhone doesn't have the horsepower for that but it doesn't need to. Since it has a gyroscope, camera motion data can be directly read. Then you can use that to simply move the crop region in each frame. Magic. It was some guy's PhD thesis at Stanford.

"To wound the autumnal city." I am thrilled that one of the books that stirred me most as an adolescent is, just this month, available as an ebook. Thursday, May 3, 2012 at 6:43pm EDT
“Bill, this is how you make money out of the music business: you do a deal with a record label. You say, ‘I’ll give you six albums, and you give me x thousand dollars.’ So, say he gets 100,000 dollars for six albums, you go out and you sign six bands, any old bands, it doesn’t matter who they are, you stick them in a studio, you record an album and you record the album for 5,000 dollars. The band will love you ’cause they get to record an album – that’s all they’ve ever wanted to do all their lives. You tell your band, ‘OK you’ve got to get it done in four or five days,’ and you get the album done. So you’ve got your six albums done for under 20,000 dollars, whatever. You’ve just made yourself 80,000 dollars. It doesn’t matter a fuck whether these records happen or not.” - Seymour Stein of Sire talking to Bill Drummond, mgr of Echo and the Bunnymen circa 1980

Wednesday, April 25, 2012 at 9:52pm EDT
Art Steinmetz added a new photo — with Ken Streb at South Bimini.
March 23, 1980. A dope smuggling plane ditched off South Bimini while we were there for a spring break dive trip. Only the tail was visible above the surface. First the locals swarmed over it with anything that floated. Then the USCG showed up and removed the bales of pot. Ken Streb, Matt Prosser and I blew off our afternoon tank dive and snorkled the 100yds out to the plane. Huge fun! Ken took the picture.

Overdiagnosis pt 7. Last one. Thanks for following this buzz kill thread. Y'all have to to choose what's right for you, of course. I do recommend this book. I don't know about medicine but I know a thing or two about statistics and behavioral economics. Doctors gotta cut and cancer terrifies us. Those facts cloud the advice we get and the judgements we make. I hope choose more wisely next time. Back to pictures of cats and what I had for dinner.

Wednesday, March 7, 2012 at 7:38am EST
Overdiagnosis pt 6. You, my 50-something facebook friend, probably have cancer. Or, rather, if you go looking for something, chances are better than 50% you will find something. As the chart below shows, what you should do about it is probably nothing. My doctor was a co-author of the "gold standard" of renal cancer treatment. "cut first, ask questions later" is the cliff notes version. This is wrong because it makes no distinction between symptomatic discoveries and incidental ones. Cheap, frequent sonograms would suffice to monitor the latter.

Monday, March 5, 2012 at 6:51pm EST
Over diagnosis pt 5. Now we get to the point of the story. My miserable post-op led me to some second guessing but what I found shocked me. For many cancers, EARLY DETECTION IS BUNK. It does not save lives. The chart below tells two stories. In 1975 50% of all kidney cancer diagnoses led to death. Now just 25% do. Is that a triumph of medicine? No. Kidney cancer deaths per 1000 are roughly unchanged. Diagnosis have soared, however. This is entirely due to "incidentalomas." we can assume that diagnosis leads to intervention. But all those interventions have not reduced the death rate at all! What they have done is created cost, cascading interventions (as in my case) and complications.

Sunday, March 4, 2012 at 12:50pm EST
Overdiagnosis pt. 4. So I go back in the hospital. Extreme pain. Internal bleeding. Stuff leaking out. Hoses of all kinds go in and get hooked up. Two pints of blood and nine days later I'm back out but with some tubes left inside and out. Turns out, some of the stuff left inside will delay the healing process. I wind up carrying around a surgical drain for five months. Going through an airport body scanner with drain bulb sticking out is awkward, I must say. Finally, the kidney seals itself. Now a YEAR LATER, I am fine but in pain from the scar and not fit for a bathing suit. Question is: was it necessary? Yes, it was a malignant cancer but so what? Some facts have emerged that suggest a diagnosis should not lead to treatment!

Friday, March 2, 2012 at 7:38pm EST
Overdiagnosis pt. 3. So, when I get done freaking out I consult with several surgeons who all say "cut." I settled on one guy who literally wrote the book on treatment protocols. He did say that 20% of such tumors are benign but this one didn't look that way although he couldn't be sure. After removal, there is only a 5% chance of recurrence, he said. So I went under the knife last November. Turns out, the tumor was malignant. The surgery went fine and three days later I went home home. Unfortunately, 3 days after that I was calling 911.

Wednesday, February 29, 2012 at 7:21pm EST
More on "Overdiagnosis." Since most of my facebook friends are of a certain age it might be useful hear my experience because I would do it differently next time. It's not one with a bad outcome but I will never know what the counterfactual is. 18 months ago I went in for my 50yr colonoscopy. It was fine. Coincidentally, I had cramps a few days earlier and when I mentioned it to the doctor he suggested a CT scan. Nothing showed up as the likely cause of my cramps but they found a 2.5cm "renal mass suggestive of malignancy." I had what doctors jokingly call an incidentaloma. Something that shows up when looking for something else, though there aren't any symptoms. Uh, oh.

Wednesday, February 29, 2012 at 7:27am EST
Ignorance of a condition may be healthier. I had part of a kidney removed a year ago. Yes, it was cancer, but doing nothing might have been the appropriate response. I'll have more to say abut this. The recent book by this op-Ed author is an eye opener and will cause many MD's to go ballistic.

Truffle-like huitlacoche (a fungus that grows on corn) is sautéed with the minty Mexican herb epazote and folded into a bubbling blend of house-made queso Oaxaca and mild asadero cheese. Ladle the resulting fusion onto warm flour tortillas with a spoonful of freshly made salsa

Sunday, September 21, 2008 at 10:42am EDT
Okay, this is one of those "you had to be there" things, but you've been there. You know how sometimes you hear a song on the radio, love it, but don't find out what it is? I don't listen to commercial radio often so it's possible for me to completely miss a hit song. I heard a song at the gym, twice, and loved it but never got the name. Then, this morning I heard it on Radio Paradise and the name scrolls across the display. Great, but the real amazing thing is I have been trying to find the song for 10 years! I heard it in 1998 and I figured it was gone forever even as the occasional riff from it came popping back into my head. It been one of those things that is slowly receeding from my memory. This moring I knew it was it after the first bar. You could have knocked me over with a feather. Like I said. you had to be there. So here is the video." Precious Little" by Eleanor McEvoy. It's fluffy pop. If you like Sarah Mclachlin, Beth Orton, etc, you might like this.
